  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e23de633-f9a8-4f00-bfc3-f445d6d8b2f0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer1377805832456908706">IN THE ETHEREAL WORLD OF THE DREAM-HUNTERS<br/>Condemned by the gods to live eternity without emotions, Arikos can only feel when he's in the dreams of others.   <span id="freeText1377805832456908706" style="display:none">IN THE ETHEREAL WORLD OF THE DREAM-HUNTERS<br />Condemned by the gods to live eternity without emotions, Arikos can only feel when he's in the dreams of others. For thousands of years, he's drifted through the human unconscious, searching for sensation. Now he's finally found a dreamer whose vivid mind can fill his emptiness.<br /><br />THERE ARE CHAMPIONS WHO FIGHT TO PROTECT THE DREAMER....<br />Dr. Megeara Kafieri watched her father ruin himself and his reputation as he searched to prove Atlantis was real. Her deathbed promise to him to salvage his reputation has now brought her to Greece where she intends to prove once and for all that the fabled island is right where her father said it was. Instead, she finds a stranger floating in the sea--one whose face she's seen many times...in her dreams.<br /><br />AND THERE ARE DEMONS WHO PREY ON THEM.<br />What she doesn't know is that Arik holds more than the ancient secrets that can help her find the mythical isle of Atlantis. He has made a pact with the god Hades: In exchange for two weeks as a mortal man, he must return to Olympus with a human soul--Megeara's.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I haven't read ALL the books in this series, but so far, yes, you can read this series in whatever order you can get your hands on them. There are tie<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I haven't read ALL the books in this series, but so far, yes, you can read this series in whatever order you can get your hands on them. There are ties between the books, but the stories also can stand alone. I hope this answer helps someone since I am answering this a bit late for you. :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300380574" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17255014122883750205"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>This was a strange world mankind lived in. No wonder they escaped into dreams.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Well, I expected more...</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387497124ra/7607490.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Aside from the secondary characters who are really worth mentioning, for me <i>The Dream-Hunter</i> was a boring, weak, and unimpressive story. <br/><br/>First of all, I have serious problems with the main characters, Arik and Geary.<br/><br/><b>Geary</b> is totally inconsistent. She is not even a character, she is just put together by various but ill-matched personalities and behaviorisms thrown in a pile. She behav</span>
  <span id="freeText17255014122883750205" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>This was a strange world mankind lived in. No wonder they escaped into dreams.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Well, I expected more...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387497124ra/7607490.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aside from the secondary characters who are really worth mentioning, for me <i>The Dream-Hunter</i> was a boring, weak, and unimpressive story. <br><br>First of all, I have serious problems with the main characters, Arik and Geary.<br><br><b>Geary</b> is totally inconsistent. She is not even a character, she is just put together by various but ill-matched personalities and behaviorisms thrown in a pile. She behaves illogically in almost every way.<br><br>First, in her approach to Atlantis... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The story starts that she hates her father because of his obsessed and vain quest for Atlantis, and considers him responsible for the death of the rest of their family. She had even changed her name in order to save her reputation and avoid all the inconveniences caused by the name of her infamous father. She not only despises her father, but she doesn’t believe in the existence of Atlantis at all. <br><br>After not meeting or speaking to each other for years, she travels to Greece to her dying father, and makes a promise to him to continue his search. She also receives artifacts from her father tagged with the date 9500 B.C., and she also identifies them – while she is standing on the shore of the Aegean Sea and her hair flies in the wind – simply looking at them as Atlantian items. Yeah, without any equipment, just because they seem <i>“very old”.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421406545ra/13372331.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Followed by a very out-of-character reasoning (something like, <i>“OMG, this stuff is from Atlantis. OMG, my father was right, OMG, I feel so guilty not believing him...”</i>), she spends six years searching for Atlantis – in vain. Towards the end of the story, she realizes that she jeopardizes her friends and family, and Arik also tells her that if she explores Atlantis, Apollymi will be free and the world is over. So she simply decides to stop searching. At least some inner conflict, please! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Second, in her behavior with Arik... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Geary is very uptight, sober, and rational, even reserved and rigid in her life. But in her dreams she is wild and passionate. I can accept this contrast. She dreams about Arik for weeks (or maybe months?) before she fishes him out of the sea. As her dreams are vivid and detailed, she knows his name, knows every aspect of his face and body, even his voice. So she saves a drowning man who looks exactly like the man from her dreams, and even his name is the same. How does she react? An archaeologist who believes in Atlantis, and knows everything about mythology, mythical beings, and gods, even dream-gods!? She suspects that he is some kind of criminal, and accuses him with nonsensical things, and treats him like shit. Her behaviour and repartees are not sarcastic, not amusing, just simply rude. She is arrogant and bitchy. <br><br>Oh, and the cliché I hate the most: the heroine’s hysteric reaction as a human to the existence of the supernatural. Well, Geary would get a prize for it. <br><br>But after Arik tells her (almost) everything, she falls for him almost immediately. Merely a couple of hours before she felt stalked by him, was in total discomfort, and suspicious about his motivations. And suddenly she is in love?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Arik</b> is boring, lame, dull, oh, just... blah... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He is obsessed with Geary but in a selfish way. He knows nothing about her, and he doesn’t even care. He just wants to meet her in the flesh and to have sex with her. Literally. Because he wants to experience it for real. He makes his careless and despicable bargain with Hades, but I despise it not only because of the fact that he offered Geary’s soul (he had no emotions at the time after all, so it quite explains it), but because at the age of twenty-seven thousand years or so, he should have at least some experience dealing with gods. He had been unemotional, not stupid! Not so believable. But of course, he can explain it.<br><blockquote><i>He always took what he wanted. Damned be the consequences. He had eternity to deal with those. What mattered most was the present, and that was what he focused on. Always.</i></blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>His emotional awakening is not consistent. Sometimes he behaves like an alien, other times he is totally adapted. <br><br>Both Arik and Geary are too weak characters to do anything on their own. They highly depend on others’ help: Solin, Zebulon (aka ZT), a Dark-Hunter named Trieg, Kat, Apollymi (she was quite helpful), Hades and Persephone. Even in the last scene, when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Geary is rescuing Arik, Kat is there to help. As soon as they get out of Hell, there is D’Alerian who shifts them back to their apartment.<br>There is only one time when Geary saves Arik from the Dolophoni changing the scene in their dreams. That was cool! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>One would expect much more from the main characters.</b> <br><br>Actually, I liked the <b>secondary characters</b> better, especially <b>Solin,</b> who was a much more complicated character than Arik. I appreciated his humor, the mystery around him, and ultimately his valor. <b>Kat</b> is a very interesting character as well. And I enjoyed <b>Tory’s</b> witty remarks, and the pourparler between <b>Hades and Persephone</b> was hilarious, even a little exaggerated. <br><br><b>The romance:</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386324ra/745771.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The plot:</b> forced. There are some fight scenes, but no real drama. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Drifting from one dream to the next, he’d been searching all these centuries for someone who could raise his emotions to the level of that first night. But no one had come close.<br>Not until Megeara. Only she was able to reach through the emptiness inside him and make him see vivid colors again. To make him feel her emotions. After all these centuries, he finally understood why certain Skoti refused to leave their partners. Why they were willing to risk death.</i>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17255014122883750205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4151687478439818867"><b>Arikos Catranides (Oneroi Skotos) and Megeara Kafieri (Human)<br/><br/>How far a man would go in order to sleep with the woman he wants…</b><br/><br/>Arik has been visiting Megeara in her dreams often. He is a dream god and an erotic Skoti. As a result, Megeara keeps having sensual dreams with intense feelings. Arik needs these sensations because, as the rest of the Skoti, he is cursed not to have any feelings and he really needs them in order to survive the nothingness of his existence. At some point, living in Megear</span>
  <span id="freeText4151687478439818867" style="display:none"><b>Arikos Catranides (Oneroi Skotos) and Megeara Kafieri (Human)<br /><br />How far a man would go in order to sleep with the woman he wants…</b><br /><br />Arik has been visiting Megeara in her dreams often. He is a dream god and an erotic Skoti. As a result, Megeara keeps having sensual dreams with intense feelings. Arik needs these sensations because, as the rest of the Skoti, he is cursed not to have any feelings and he really needs them in order to survive the nothingness of his existence. At some point, living in Megeara’s dreams will not be enough. Thus, he will try to live like a mortal for a while in order to meet her. Hades will help, but not without a bargain.<br /><br />Geary Kafieri is on a quest to discover the lost Atlantis somewhere close to Santorini and clear her father’s name until she discovers the man of her dreams (literally) floating unconscious in the sea.<br /><br />The story was a bit slow-paced (especially during the first part of the book), but it was full of mythology and the story really takes off after a while. I thought the secondary characters were more interesting than the main characters:<br />1.Solin Catranides. Arik’s brother/half brother/cousin/fellow god. Anyway, Arik’s relative.<br />2.Katra Agrotera. One of Artemis’ koris who needs to stop Geary from discovering Atlantis.<br />3.Zebulon. The powerful Chthonian more than 27,542 years ago who can destroy even gods.<br /><br />I wish the writer had described in more details <br />-the surprise of Geary, when she discovers that gods are real and <br />-how Arik feels when he is human.<br />…But overall I don’t have any complains. I can surely imagine Gods and Goddesses walking in Fira’s alleys in Santorini.<br /><br />Note: I usually don’t bother correcting Greek language mistakes in English texts that are trying to translate greek, but I feel the need to do it this time because the meaning is totally different. So, Zebulon’s T-shirt says:<br />“Σας προσέχω, είμαι φοβισμένος” but it should really say:<br />“Σας παρακολουθώ γι’ αυτό να φοβάστε”, which is the exact translation of<br /> “I am watching you, be afraid.”</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7926688452407010120">The 1st book in the Dream-Hunter Series which is also part of the Dark Series World….okay, you’re confused…so am I!!! All these “inside” series of a series!!! Ok, never mind…enough of that!!!<br/><br/>Dark-Hunters job is to protect humans from demons entering their dreams. This is the story of a once powerful member of the Oneroi who fell from grace!!!!<blockquote>
  
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437581204i/15599678.jpg' alt=' photo Jj1bs_zpskqnvziap.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  
</blockquote> <br/>Arik was one of those protectors but things went wrong when he entered a human’s dream, resulting in him becoming a Skotos, losing all his fee</span>
  <span id="freeText7926688452407010120" style="display:none">The 1st book in the Dream-Hunter Series which is also part of the Dark Series World….okay, you’re confused…so am I!!! All these “inside” series of a series!!! Ok, never mind…enough of that!!!<br><br>Dark-Hunters job is to protect humans from demons entering their dreams. This is the story of a once powerful member of the Oneroi who fell from grace!!!!<blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437581204i/15599678.jpg" alt=" photo Jj1bs_zpskqnvziap.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  
</blockquote> <br>Arik was one of those protectors but things went wrong when he entered a human’s dream, resulting in him becoming a Skotos, losing all his feelings and has been for thousands of years looking for someone that will make him feel passion and alive again. <br>But then he enters into a human woman’s sensual chocolate dream – yes, not kidding….<blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437581204i/15599679.jpg" alt=" photo images_zpstwinbon7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  
</blockquote>This is someone who makes him see the vivid colors and feel emotions that he believed were gone forever!!!! <br><br>Megeara Kafieri, pure Atlantean blood in her, anthropologist and underwater recovery expert… ….<blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437581204i/15599680.jpg" alt=" photo geary-145x145_zpsqoefjwqp.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  
</blockquote><br>She travels to Greece, determined to finding the fabled lost civilization of Atlantis….<blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437581204i/15599681.jpg" alt=" photo hqdefault_zps7prn8y4s.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  
</blockquote>to vindicate her dead father’s reputation that was left in tatters when he had not been able to prove it whilst he was still alive.<br><br>This was not a bad book but it never really wowed me!!!<br><br>Arik was a bit of a pain….selfish, self-centered…caring for no one but himself. He does redeem himself a bit at the end when he actually sacrifices himself for Megeara…who by the way he had barter her life for his curse to be broken!!!!<br><br>Megeara was so whiny and painful at times…that I wanted to throttle her!!! Oh, she wasn’t pretty enough for someone as awesome as Arik…what is it with these human females that the Dark Hunters fall in love with always have ….I am not gorgeous enough for this “gorgeouness “guy!!!!!! Get a life girls!!!!!<br><br>I found the secondary characters and subplots much more interesting than the romance between Arik &amp; Megeara!!! A lot of this series characters make an appearance and the interaction and dialogue is awesome as usual…..loved seeing Kat &amp; her beyond “cruella” mother Apollymi… And loved, loved the Greek Islands setting.<br><br>I liked it but this is not going to be a reread soon!!!!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1458408654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9120673641170952114">Oh prequels. I'm not a fan. Sorry!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449213093i/17252443.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>*shudder* Not even once...</i><br/><br/>This takes place before all of the other books. And, it isn't about a Dark hunter, but a Dream Hunter which is a lot less exciting. I don't know how other people feel on this, but I don't really like when books have a bunch of dreams written in them. I get really bored really fast and start skimming. I feel the same way about people telling me about a dream they had. Dreams don't make sense, okay? And, you struggling to tell me how the </span>
  <span id="freeText9120673641170952114" style="display:none">Oh prequels. I'm not a fan. Sorry!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449213093i/17252443.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>*shudder* Not even once...</i><br><br>This takes place before all of the other books. And, it isn't about a Dark hunter, but a Dream Hunter which is a lot less exciting. I don't know how other people feel on this, but I don't really like when books have a bunch of dreams written in them. I get really bored really fast and start skimming. I feel the same way about people telling me about a dream they had. Dreams don't make sense, okay? And, you struggling to tell me how the pig turned into your mother and you were running from a buffalo isn't interesting to me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449213218i/17252467.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Needless to say, I found this book very boring. I didn't care about either character, who had a pre-existing relationship by being "dream lovers", and I didn't care about the main plot. The only good thing about this book was the glimpses of Ash and the tiny, minuscule glimpses of the Dark Hunters before the first book. But, overall, totally not worth trudging through to get those small gems.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449213013i/17252437._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1329774963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1329774963" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1329774963?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1329774963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5967456033567412950">This was another great installment in the Dark-Hunter series. Though I guess this was really a Dream-Hunter book. It had the usual mix of romance, humor, and action that you would expect from the series, and also included some interesting subplots as well as an interesting main story arc.<br/><br/>Arik is an emotionless Skotos who only feels emotions when he drains them from humans in their dreams. When he encounters the dreams of the Atlantis seeking Megeara Kafieri he is drawn to her unlike any human he</span>
  <span id="freeText5967456033567412950" style="display:none">This was another great installment in the Dark-Hunter series. Though I guess this was really a Dream-Hunter book. It had the usual mix of romance, humor, and action that you would expect from the series, and also included some interesting subplots as well as an interesting main story arc.<br /><br />Arik is an emotionless Skotos who only feels emotions when he drains them from humans in their dreams. When he encounters the dreams of the Atlantis seeking Megeara Kafieri he is drawn to her unlike any human he has encountered before. The pull is so great that when the Oneroi block him visiting her dreams Arik strikes a bargain with Hades that will see him become human for two weeks. During that time he will be able to live and feel emotions like a regular human. The price of this bargain is Megeara's soul! The price seemed like nothing at all to Arik when he had no feelings and emotions, but the longer he spends in the human world, with Megeara, the more he realizes the true price of the bargain he has struck with Hades. <br /><br />I enjoyed the romance between Arik and Geary. It was totally different to any of the other romances in the series so far. It started out as only a physical attraction between the pair and then developed into true feelings as the spent real time with each other and got to know each other better. Megeara was likable enough even if she was not one of the series more memorable characters. It was interesting to follow Arik's development over the course of the story as he was initially quite unlikable due to his lack of feeling and concern for others. Luckily the more time he spent as a human and feeling emotions the more likable he got. The romance also held plenty of humor as Arik was unaccustomed to being in the human world and dealing with all the rules and social niceties that went with it. The banter between Arik and his half brother Solin was utterly hilarious. <br /><br />The plot itself was fairly intriguing. Hades deal gave Arik two weeks on earth as a human, but some of the other Gods and his Oneroi brothers had their own reasons for wanting him dead before that time limit expired. Then their was Megeara and her families quest to find Atlantis. A quest that proved dangerous as none of the Greek Gods want the site found and Apollymi's imprisonment disturbed. <br /><br />Another real plus for this book was that we got to meet a whole bunch of interesting new secondary characters like the Oneroi leaders M'Ordant, D'Alerian, and M'Adoc, and a few more of the Greek Gods in the form of Hades and Persephone. The real standout secondary characters were the awesome Solin, Kat, and ZT, who all definitely deserve books of their own! <br /><br />All in all I was really happy with this installment. <br /><br />Rating: 4 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: This was narrated by Fred Berman. He does a great job as always with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5967456033567412950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_391368323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/391368323" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391368323?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391368323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1030189640297041518">I really liked this book. It seems that a lot of people don’t like the addition of the Dream Hunters to the Dark Hunter series, but I found the concept an intriguing one - a race that is cursed to feel no emotions and therefore have to syphon them off humans while they dream. It puts a whole new spin on Sherrilyn Kenyon’s world, and how everything is interwoven. <br/><br/>In this story we meet Dream Hunter, Arik. He is infatuated with Megeara/Geary, whose (very HOT) dreams he has been sharing, so hot that</span>
  <span id="freeText1030189640297041518" style="display:none">I really liked this book. It seems that a lot of people don’t like the addition of the Dream Hunters to the Dark Hunter series, but I found the concept an intriguing one - a race that is cursed to feel no emotions and therefore have to syphon them off humans while they dream. It puts a whole new spin on Sherrilyn Kenyon’s world, and how everything is interwoven. <br /><br />In this story we meet Dream Hunter, Arik. He is infatuated with Megeara/Geary, whose (very HOT) dreams he has been sharing, so hot that he makes a deal with Hades to spend two weeks on earth as a human to be with her – for a price. Geary, meanwhile, is on a mission to continue her family legacy and find the lost city of Atlantis – which leads to all sorts of issues for the gods who want to keep both it, and the trapped Apollymi, a secret. <br /><br />I suspect part of the reason people don’t like this book as much is because Arik is not exactly a strong Alpha male like we are used to from earlier books. But it completely suited his character and the situation he was in. I really liked his innocence, and watching him discover the world as a ‘human’ as he was finally exposed to the emotions that he had never been allowed to feel as a Dream Hunter. <br /><br />Geary is a strong heroine. Fiercely protective of her family and friends, and eventually of Arik, she has a wickedly dry sense of humour and I really liked her. <br /><br />Like the other books in the series, there is a big cast of supporting characters – almost all of which we hadn’t met before. Highlights for me were Kat, the mysterious handmaiden of Artemis (who we met briefly - and somewhat bizarrely - in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84144.Seize_the_Night__Dark_Hunter___7_" title="Seize the Night (Dark-Hunter, #7) by Sherrilyn Kenyon" rel="nofollow noopener">Seize the Night</a>), Geary’s cousin Tory - the genius yet sassy teenager who reads Plato for fun, Solin and his banter with Arik, which was brilliant, the oh-so-sarcastic Zebulon and the introduction of Hades and his wife Persephone – they were hilarious! <br /><br />There wasn’t as much action in this book, but there was definitely some excitement, and lots of swoon - and a very sappy epilogue :) There was a heavy focus on the mythology which I really enjoyed, and I believe is setting us up for future books in the series (including another reveal on the deliciously mysterious Acheron). <br /><br />I love how I can easily fall back into Kenyon’s world whenever I pick one of her books up. Like other favourite authors of mine, you always know what you’re going to get in her stories, and she never disappoints. <br /><br />On a side note – since reading this book and doing a bit of research, I’ve discovered that some of the characters we meet in this story have books of their own coming and OMFG!!! I cannot WAIT to get to those stories, and the secrets that they hold. Squeee!!!!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1030189640297041518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1428040586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428040586" />
    <a title="Alp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26653561-alp"><img alt="Alp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462791280p2/26653561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1428040586?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alp" href="/user/show/26653561-alp">Alp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1428040586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13496222238469641194">Sherrilyn Kenyon is one of my favorite authors whose books I never get bored of. I love how she has weaved the Greek mythology and history into her Fantasy-Paranormal Romance stories. Although the first half of the book was a bit slow, the story picked up greatly in the second half.<br/><br/>This is the first book in Dream-Hunter series, the story of Arikos or Arik, the Skoti who was drawn to the heroine’s rich and sensational dreamscapes, and Dr. Megeara or Geary, the woman who was trying to prove that A</span>
  <span id="freeText13496222238469641194" style="display:none">Sherrilyn Kenyon is one of my favorite authors whose books I never get bored of. I love how she has weaved the Greek mythology and history into her Fantasy-Paranormal Romance stories. Although the first half of the book was a bit slow, the story picked up greatly in the second half.<br /><br />This is the first book in Dream-Hunter series, the story of Arikos or Arik, the Skoti who was drawn to the heroine’s rich and sensational dreamscapes, and Dr. Megeara or Geary, the woman who was trying to prove that Atlantis was not just a myth.<br /><br />5 Stars for the storyline. It was so entertaining and the characters were well developed. I liked that the supporting characters were not less important / interesting than the protagonists. The fight scenes were so good, almost stole my breath. But my only complaint with this book was the romance--2 stars for this part. I was quite disappointed with the lack of chemistry between Arik and Geary, and when they fell in love with each other, it happened way too abruptly! However, I was very impressed with the conclusion and the ending of the book.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Laughing, he pulled her into his arms and held her close. "Thank you, Geary." <br />"For what?" <br />"For giving me a life that is the best dream I've ever had."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />All in all, I enjoyed reading this book for the most part. The story quite delivered on its promise. My first intention was to give this book 3 stars but the last quarter pushed it up to 4!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13496222238469641194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_840889197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840889197" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/840889197?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Romance fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=published2007">published2007</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer840889197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4899316826844875000">Kenyon is keeping my head spinning by interspersing books that are actually enjoyable with books that are horrible. This is one of the enjoyable ones.<br/><br/>Arik is a Skotos, meaning he's an emotionless dream-god who feeds off people's emotions by visiting them in dreams. He's been having dream-sex with Geary (Dr. Megeara (Saatsakis) Kafieri) for two months now.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, dream-gods aren't supposed to spend that much time with one human - only one or two nights and then move on. So Arik is warned t</span>
  <span id="freeText4899316826844875000" style="display:none">Kenyon is keeping my head spinning by interspersing books that are actually enjoyable with books that are horrible. This is one of the enjoyable ones.<br /><br />Arik is a Skotos, meaning he's an emotionless dream-god who feeds off people's emotions by visiting them in dreams. He's been having dream-sex with Geary (Dr. Megeara (Saatsakis) Kafieri) for two months now.<br /><br />Unfortunately, dream-gods aren't supposed to spend that much time with one human - only one or two nights and then move on. So Arik is warned to stop visiting Geary.<br /><br />In order to have more time with her, Arik goes to Hades to ask to be turned into a human so that he can meet Geary and spend time with her. Being human will give him a full range of vibrant emotions and also he'll be able to taste, smell, feel - all the fun stuff humans get to do in the real world. In exchange for giving Arik two weeks on Earth as a human, Hades wants Geary's soul. At the end of the two week period, Arik will kill Geary and give Hades her soul. He makes this deal without hesitation - he has no feelings and certainly doesn't love Geary.<br /><br />However, that all changes once he's plunged into the emotionally fraught human world...<br />...<br /><br />Geary is on a quest to find the lost city of Atlantis. She sees a man drowning in the ocean one night when she is out on her boat. Imagine her surprise when the man she drags out of the water turns out to be the man she's used to seeing naked in her dreams...<br />...<br /><br />This book was very satisfying. It was fun to see Arik struggle with human emotions, and discover things like Reese's Peanut Butter Cups. It was also amusing to see him grappling with human niceties and manners. The reader also gets to see him turn from a total emotionless, selfish creep into someone who cares for others and learns to feel compassion. I am a sucker for these kinds of stories. :)<br /><br />Kenyon also borrows heavily from classic Greek mythology here (in a way that is reminiscent of a PERCY JACKSON book) and that is also something that I enjoy. We spend time with Hades, Persephone, and other famous Greek characters in this book.<br /><br />There's action and fighting, love and sex, redemption, - all the stuff I really want in a romance novel.<br /><br />Really the only bad thing I can say about it is that Kenyon yet again just CANNOT resist slipping in this female self-hatred. Geary is by all accounts an attractive woman, yet she cannot stop dissing herself and making negative comments about how unattractive she is. This is SO tiring and SUCH a turn-off for me. Women with low self-esteem drive me NUTS.<br /><br />If you took out that part, this was actually a novel that left me satisfied and happy. It had a good plot and interesting characters.<br /><br />3 REAL STARS, 4 ROMANCE STARS</span>
  <a data-text-id="4899316826844875000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1192545350" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192545350" />
    <a title="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed"><img alt="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455042547p2/22911953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192545350?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" href="/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed">Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=greek-roman-mythology">greek-roman-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192545350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer164479010913786522">This is the first book of the Dream-Hunters, but they've made appearances already in the Dark-Hunter books. The story predates all the DH & Were-Hunter books (if you're reading them in the author's DH Universe suggested order). The prologue is in 1994 & the story in 1996. That I've already read 17 books/stories in the DH universe & know what's going to happen, this book was super annoying. <b> 1.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Plot: Geary has a ph.d in history - ancient civilizations and comes from a long line of Atlantis </span>
  <span id="freeText164479010913786522" style="display:none">This is the first book of the Dream-Hunters, but they've made appearances already in the Dark-Hunter books. The story predates all the DH &amp; Were-Hunter books (if you're reading them in the author's DH Universe suggested order). The prologue is in 1994 &amp; the story in 1996. That I've already read 17 books/stories in the DH universe &amp; know what's going to happen, this book was super annoying. <b> 1.5 stars</b><br /><br />Plot: Geary has a ph.d in history - ancient civilizations and comes from a long line of Atlantis searchers. Most of her family perished in the search for the lost city &amp; she left Greece as a teenager to pursue her own life. She doesn't believe in Atlantis &amp; hates that her family is dead, but she made a promise to her father on his deathbed to finish his quest &amp; find the city. This becomes her obsession, clearing her father's name &amp; reputation, showing that he wasn't crazy. <br /><br />Arikos, a Dream-Hunter meets Geary in her dreams &amp; falls in lust with her, continuing a dream lust relationship with her for weeks, until he becomes restless for more. Arikos wants to know her in the real world, not in the misty dream world. He makes a deal &amp; ends up human for 2 weeks &amp; finds out dream world Geary is much different from real world Geary. She's inhibited &amp; consumed with her quest, not jumping his bones like she does in dreams. <br /><br />Thoughts: First half to 3/4's of the book were boring. It was all Geary consumed with finding Atlantis, no matter what, ignoring everything else. Literally, her inner monologue was all "must find Atlantis, must find it, must find it." Really boring. Even when Arik, in all his godly perfection of male hotness shows up, she's still thinking about Atlantis 98% of the time. Arik tries to befriend her, but she disses him until he gets her diving permits - with the bargain that he could come along in the boat if he obtained them. What follows is more of her being an annoying twit &amp; Arik trying to understand humans. There's also no real villain or plot. <br /><br />Geary is annoying &amp; Arik is meh, until the end. The last 1/4th or so of the book is good and made me like the main characters. Geary grows a brain &amp; Arik realizes he has a heart &amp; true human feelings. Enjoyed the rescue, solution, &amp; those who gave aid. But knowing the why's about not finding Atlantis &amp; how disastrous it would be, made reading this with Geary's obsession as fun as eating rocks. I wanted to kill her for her stupidity &amp; Arik for helping, since he knew better. <br /><br />Other characters: <br />Kat - Like her, happy to have learned more about her. <br />Apollymi: Like her much much much better than the heifer goddess (Artemis). <br />Tory: Fun &amp; loved her genius brain, stats spouting self. <br />Thia: waste of space. <br />Solin: I liked his anti-hero personality. <br />Zebulon: Please let him have his own book. It would be awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="164479010913786522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

As always Persephone and Hades are my favs. What's annoying is the subseries get confusing. Did I read this in order?Not sure. Overall, not bad. Loved the Euridice and Orpheus reference. Good thing I don't mind loads of characters. They are all interesting, and the plot twists aren't bad. Just wish I liked Geary more and loved Arik less.</span>

<div id="review_35546175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35546175" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35546175?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-in-pursuit">hero-in-pursuit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=antihero">antihero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35546175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2870104270814683658">The Dream Hunter was a book that I got completely sucked into by page one. It takes the Dark Hunter series in a different direction, and shines the spotlight on yet another group of gods in the pantheon of Sherrilyn Kenyon's Dark Hunter universe. I loved how SK integrated the dream world into this book. Dreams are so complex and so fantastical, how could they not be an excellent backdrop for an epic war between good and evil? SK gets that the Greek myths have characters that are not always compl</span>
  <span id="freeText2870104270814683658" style="display:none">The Dream Hunter was a book that I got completely sucked into by page one. It takes the Dark Hunter series in a different direction, and shines the spotlight on yet another group of gods in the pantheon of Sherrilyn Kenyon's Dark Hunter universe. I loved how SK integrated the dream world into this book. Dreams are so complex and so fantastical, how could they not be an excellent backdrop for an epic war between good and evil? SK gets that the Greek myths have characters that are not always completely good or evil, that the gods' motivations are often selfish and petty. We see that Arikos is not a bad guy. He's merely a person who has tired of being abused as used as a pawn by the higher gods. He wants happiness and joy just like all us humans want. The closest he has come is through the dreams of the human Megeara. When he is denied the closeness he craves with her through the dreams, he desperately makes a deal with Hades to be human for two weeks to spend time with this human he has become so captivated with. Unfortunately the deal involves giving her up to Hades after the two weeks ends. However, those of us who have studied the myths know that the gods don't make fair deals. Arik says yes before he realizes what the caveat is.<br />The Dream Hunter introduces new intriguing characters and allows us to reconnect with some old favorites. The time line is about 10 years in the past, which is interesting, as we get to see the time before some pretty big events unfold. <br />I love this world, and even if there's not much going on, I'd read SK's books just to experience her incredible imagination, and her fantastic writing ability. However, this book does have a lot going on, passion, pathos, vengeance, adventure, fun, and excitement. Also for those of you like me who has a thing for Atlantis, there is a quest to find the lost city that many don't want found, as well. You don't want to put it down because you want to know what happens next. I loved the direction that SK went with this book because it gives me some in depth on some of the Greek myths that always intrigued me. She brings these gods and heroes of the myths to life for me, but also adds her own unique spin that makes me laugh at some times, and cry at others.<br />This is not a Dark Hunter book in the traditional sense, but it is definitely a great addition to the mythos, and if you are a fan of SK's books, I have trouble believing you won't love this book as well. Let me close by saying I hope that Solin gets his own book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2870104270814683658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_714963294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/714963294" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/714963294?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749956363" href="/book/show/13763838-the-dream-hunter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=for-review-read">for-review-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer714963294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer75585213348186614">I'm a huge fan of <b>Sherrilyn Kenyon</b> and the Dark-Hunters series but unfortunately this was my least favourite book in the series so far. Having said that it's probably still better than a lot of paranormal romance stories out there but I have high expectations when I pick up a book by this author and for some reason <b>The Dream-Hunter</b> didn't quite live up to them.<br/><br/>I did really enjoy finding out about the Dream Hunters and learning about their abilities but I was put off Arik because of his initial a</span>
  <span id="freeText75585213348186614" style="display:none">I'm a huge fan of <b>Sherrilyn Kenyon</b> and the Dark-Hunters series but unfortunately this was my least favourite book in the series so far. Having said that it's probably still better than a lot of paranormal romance stories out there but I have high expectations when I pick up a book by this author and for some reason <b>The Dream-Hunter</b> didn't quite live up to them.<br /><br />I did really enjoy finding out about the Dream Hunters and learning about their abilities but I was put off Arik because of his initial attitude towards Geary. He thought nothing of signing away her soul if it meant he got to spend 2 weeks as a human living with her and being able to experience real emotions and I find that kind of thing hard to forgive in my heroes. Admittedly Arik does change his mind and I was glad that he was willing to risk so much to keep her safe once he started to have feelings for her but by that point I wasn't as head over heels in love with him as I have been with all of SK's other heroes.<br /><br />I liked Geary and I enjoyed finding out about her family's history and their search for Atlantis but I found her hard to connect to and I had a hard time buying into her relationship with Arik. The connection between them seemed to be more about their chemistry than any deeper emotional bond. I think I was actually more interested in the various side plots than I was in the main romance which is disappointing. I still enjoy this author's writing style, I love the richly developed and diverse world of the Dark-Hunters, she never seems to run out of new mythology to pull into the series and that side of things is just as fascinating as ever. The Dream-Hunter may not have been my favourite book but it hasn't put be off continuing the series and I have high hopes that <b>Fear the Darkness</b> will be as good or better than the earlier books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="75585213348186614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_459113916" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459113916" />
    <a title="Sammy Loves Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14227114-sammy-loves-books"><img alt="Sammy Loves Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534119573p2/14227114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459113916?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sammy Loves Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sammy Loves Books" href="/user/show/14227114-sammy-loves-books">Sammy Loves Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14227114-sammy-loves-books?shelf=greek-gods">greek-gods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14227114-sammy-loves-books?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459113916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3094039640572202662">I hesitated to write a review for this book because though I enjoyed some parts, I found the majority of the book slow and filled with repetitive information that fans of the Dark Hunter series would already know. Arik is a likable hero because he's a rule breaking bad ass that can fight. He is also willing to trade his life for the woman he loves. Arik was lost in the real world and needed guidance from his brother Solin in wooing Geary. Solin is a very interesting character with a dark past th</span>
  <span id="freeText3094039640572202662" style="display:none">I hesitated to write a review for this book because though I enjoyed some parts, I found the majority of the book slow and filled with repetitive information that fans of the Dark Hunter series would already know. Arik is a likable hero because he's a rule breaking bad ass that can fight. He is also willing to trade his life for the woman he loves. Arik was lost in the real world and needed guidance from his brother Solin in wooing Geary. Solin is a very interesting character with a dark past that I hope to see more of in the future.<br /><br />I didn't care much for the heroine, Geary, being so uptight and suspicious throughout the entire book. She was wound so tight that the first and only love scene takes place around page 240. So after months of hot dream loving, Geary couldn't bring herself to make love to Arik in reality till the book was about over. Heck even 15 year old Tory doesn't understand why she didn't stay up deck with him in his hammock. I wish writers could understand that dream sequence love scenes don't count because they aren't real!<br /><br />I enjoyed the fight between Kat and Artemis over her relationship with Apollymi. There was a little more background info on Apollymi but so much of the info was repetitive that it was boring. Apollymi's mental discussions with Geary shed new light on the goddess. She isn't 100% evil. She has a soft side. I was glad to finally be introduced to Tory. I know who she is and what she will become in future books so it was nice meet and like her character.<br /><br />I would have given this book a 3 star but I fell asleep twice while reading and had to skim a lot of the repetitive stuff. Then to find that even though this book is #10 in the series, Zarek is still in Alaska, Nick is still a skate board riding kid working for the dark hunter, Kyrian. This book could have been a prequel to the entire series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3094039640572202662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1816149918" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816149918" />
    <a title="Sandra ~ ♥ Cross My Heart ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart"><img alt="Sandra ~ ♥ Cross My Heart ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415483040p2/17716247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1816149918?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra ~ ♥ Cross My Heart ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra ~ ♥ Cross My Heart ♥" href="/user/show/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart">Sandra ~ ♥ Cross My Heart ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6606291-the-dream-hunter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart?shelf=pnr-vampires">pnr-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart?shelf=bewitching-book-covers">bewitching-book-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart?shelf=pnr-other">pnr-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart?shelf=romance-pnr">romance-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17716247-sandra-cross-my-heart?shelf=pnr-angels-demons">pnr-angels-demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1816149918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17563584371335291191">I'm a fan of the Dark Hunters - Dark, damaged, bad*ss alpha males hunting Daemons & protecting mankind - all with intriguing backstories. BBF/Hero material. While Dream Hunter Arik, is certainly damaged and on the high end of the SexOmeter - I had some trouble feeling empathy with him in the same way as I have the Dark Hunters. The story was slow to draw me in as I missed some of the intensity of other books in the series.<br/><br/>Arik bargains with Hades for two weeks as a human in order to experience s</span>
  <span id="freeText17563584371335291191" style="display:none">I'm a fan of the Dark Hunters - Dark, damaged, bad*ss alpha males hunting Daemons &amp; protecting mankind - all with intriguing backstories. BBF/Hero material. While Dream Hunter Arik, is certainly damaged and on the high end of the SexOmeter - I had some trouble feeling empathy with him in the same way as I have the Dark Hunters. The story was slow to draw me in as I missed some of the intensity of other books in the series.<br /><br />Arik bargains with Hades for two weeks as a human in order to experience sex for real with Megeara “Geary” Saatsakis, a woman whose dreams Arik has invaded - hot, steamy, erotic dreams. Dream Hunters are forbidden to remain in one person's dreams multiple times, and Arik is ordered to move on to someone else but refuses. Geary is searching for Atlantis to restore her dead father's reputation as he had been ridiculed in life and after death for believing it existed. Arik received a box from her father - he left her proof in the form of an ancient coin. When Arik &amp; Geary meet in the human realm, Arik offers to help Geary get the needed permits to begin her search. She recognizes Arik from her dreams, but doesn't know that it's her soul that he traded to Hades in a deal for two weeks as a human. <br /><br />As this story plays out, there are some humorous moments as Arik fumbles the finer details of being human. But I wanted to feel more chemistry between Arik and Geary. I found the Atlantis plot line intriguing and the supporting cast interesting - ranging from egotistical Greek Gods to some snarky characters to Arik's brother, and they all helped carry the story. While certainly unique, <i>Dream Hunter</i> moved a bit slow for me until near the end. Most certainly a different and interesting addition to the series. A Must Read for fans of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17563584371335291191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer186044826729660990">A very interesting read, this story was actually focused more on the mythology of Atlantis than the rest of the books in this series. The romance between Geary (Human) and Arik (Dream Hunter/Skotos) was sweet.<br/><br/>Appoloymi comes real close to being released from her prision because of Geary's discovery of where Atlantis is located beneath the sea but thanks to Katra, Solin, and Arik, Appoloymi remains in her prision.<br/><br/>However now, Geary knows the truth behind Atlantis and about all the immortals. I th</span>
  <span id="freeText186044826729660990" style="display:none">A very interesting read, this story was actually focused more on the mythology of Atlantis than the rest of the books in this series. The romance between Geary (Human) and Arik (Dream Hunter/Skotos) was sweet.<br /><br />Appoloymi comes real close to being released from her prision because of Geary's discovery of where Atlantis is located beneath the sea but thanks to Katra, Solin, and Arik, Appoloymi remains in her prision.<br /><br />However now, Geary knows the truth behind Atlantis and about all the immortals. I thought it was interesting how Geary goes through Hades to get Arik back. I love a happy ending. She even turns out pregnant in the end.<br /><br />I noticed the book was out of sink in the time line of this story because it mentions sending a dream hunter to Zarek in Alaska to learn compassion and also mentions Kyran and Nick, only Kyran is not mated yet and is still a Dark Hunter.<br /><br />I look forward to reading the next book in this series.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73076186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4943767650589197102">Not crazy about this one. It took me a long time to finish it, because the plot just wasn't very interesting. I didn't care about either of the main characters, Megeara and Arik. The love story between them felt flat and fake, and I really didn't care if they ended up together. It finally got a little bit interesting toward the end, and I credit that to some of the minor characters, like Kat and Solin. This is the first of Kenyon's books that I have read, so maybe some of her other stuf is good.</span>
  <span id="freeText4943767650589197102" style="display:none">Not crazy about this one. It took me a long time to finish it, because the plot just wasn't very interesting. I didn't care about either of the main characters, Megeara and Arik. The love story between them felt flat and fake, and I really didn't care if they ended up together. It finally got a little bit interesting toward the end, and I credit that to some of the minor characters, like Kat and Solin. This is the first of Kenyon's books that I have read, so maybe some of her other stuf is good. I don't know, but I doubt I'll be rushing out to give her another shot.<br />On a totally different note, I hate the cover. The guy himself isn't bad-looking, but what's up with that freaky hair?! Is it a wig? Is it a bad perm? Did they flip it upside down and tease it? Ugh!<br />While I'm at it, the Don Jonson/Miami Vice stubble doesn't do it for me either.</span>

<div id="review_1294747009" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1294747009" />
    <a title="Lover of Romance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance"><img alt="Lover of Romance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458253423p2/3709091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1294747009?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lover of Romance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lover of Romance" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance">Lover of Romance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=genre-mythology">genre-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1294747009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14152601307787453665">Summary <br/>Arik, is a Dream Hunter, and as one he is cursed to never feel emotion but then he enters into Megeara dreams….a dream where she is bathing in a waterfall of chocolate. Ever since he is captivated by Megeara, a human woman who for some reason can resist his call to enter the dream world when she doesn’t choose to. When he is ordered to stop entering her dreams, he goes to the god Hades and makes a deal with him, that in order to be human for a few weeks, he will have to give Hades Megear</span>
  <span id="freeText14152601307787453665" style="display:none">Summary <br />Arik, is a Dream Hunter, and as one he is cursed to never feel emotion but then he enters into Megeara dreams….a dream where she is bathing in a waterfall of chocolate. Ever since he is captivated by Megeara, a human woman who for some reason can resist his call to enter the dream world when she doesn’t choose to. When he is ordered to stop entering her dreams, he goes to the god Hades and makes a deal with him, that in order to be human for a few weeks, he will have to give Hades Megeara’s soul or give up his own. So Arik agrees, all he knows is he needs her and will do anything to have her. Megeara is searching for the city of Atlantis, and most of her life she never believed in the search, and it cost almost every member of her family’s life, but then she made a promise to her father on his deathbed to not give up and redeem their family name, no matter the cost to herself. But when her dream man comes ashore naked from the ocean, she is suspicious and she knows he is keeping secrets, but she can’t deny the attraction she feels for him. But soon she will be drawn into a dangerous world, a world that could cause her death for getting too close to the infamous city of Atlantis.<br /><br />The Hero <br />Arik, is part of the many dream hunters. Arik, along with many of his other brethren, are cursed to never feel emotion. Because centuries previous, one of their kind, decided to play a game on Zeus and they all pay for it now. Arik is a man who has never felt emotion except when he enters the dream world with Megeara, and he knew that the moment he made that deal with Hades, that he had made a mistake. Arik doesn’t know what he will do when his time is up, and he realizes that he will have to give up his own life for her, because Megeara is everything good and pure in the world, and when he realizes that he loves her…he will do everything in his power to protect her.<br /><br />The Heroine<br />Megeara, hated her childhood, she never was able to enjoy it, because her family was obsessed with finding “atlantis”. She lost just about her family member, and now she only has one cousin left alive. But she made a promise to her father, and as she found certain artifacts of his, she starts to realize that Atlantis is real, and she must find it if only to redeem her family’s name, so that they didn’t die for nothing. Megeara is intelligent and passionate, and has certain gifts that are more than the average human. What was most enjoyable about Megeara is how she stands up to Arik, a god of dreams, and she has such a zest for what she believes in and I loved seeing her character develop through the story.<br /><br />Plot and Story Line <br />Dream Hunter is the first book in the Dream Hunter series. My local state has an audio book library, and I found this treasure available, and since I have yet to read the series, I thought that I needed to give it a try. This book was a riot of fun, passion and some Greek adventure. This series is connected to the Dark Hunter series, and we see in this book and other books in the series, connection to characters to the Dark Hunter series. Dream Hunter is a story that just won my heart over from the beginning, And the narrator, is one that from what I have seen has done most of the books in these connecting series, and he is fantastic. It is rare for me to love a male narrator, since I have mostly listened to female narrators, but he is one of the best I have ever listened to. I loved the way this story develops, and it has some twists that are unexpected, and boy was I surprised over a few things, and what became most endearing was seeing how these two fight for a future together. Dream Hunter is a story that won me over, with these charming characters, a story line that is packed with adventure, greek gods, and a romance that is bound to captivate you. What was most provocative about this story was seeing the way these two come to fight for one another. Arik, who at first is conceited and arrogant, but when he learns the error of his ways is willing to give up his own soul for the woman he loves. Then we have Megeara, when she learns the complete truth about Arik, she goes to drastic lengths to bring him back to her, even if that means facing Hades herself, loved the courage and tenacity and the will to be together. The supporting characters are quite fun and added a certain flair to the story that gave the story the humorous edge it needed.<br /><br />The Cover <br />I really like this cover, and it connects with the story, and boy can I say that man is HOT and sexy!! Those eyes….I would have him in a heartbeat, and the hair….he is one delicious package.<br /><br />Overall View<br />Dream Hunter is a story to grab at you and will refuse to let go….its a action packed story that is bound to have you on edge in anticipation of what is to come, a book to captivate and charm every reader!! A MUST Read for fans of the Dark Hunters Series, or who love a romance that is sensual and emotionally provoking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14152601307787453665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=vamps">vamps</a>,
